            function wpSolutionToggle(solution, link, showtext, hidetext) {
                if (solution.style.display != 'none') {
                    solution.style.display = 'none';
                    link.innerHTML = showtext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_show';
                } else {
                    solution.style.display = 'block';
                    link.innerHTML = hidetext;
                    link.className = 'solution_link_hide';
                }
            }

<script type="text/javascript">
//<![CDATA[



/* JQUERY */
jQuery(document).ready(function(){ 
    
   
  

	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish(); */
	/* jQuery('ul#rmenu').superfish().find('ul').bgIframe({opacity:false}); */
 
	/* For IE6 */
	if (jQuery.browser.msie && /MSIE 6\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 7\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent) && !/MSIE 8\.0/i.test(window.navigator.userAgent)) {

		/* Max-width for images in IE6 */		
		var centerwidth = jQuery("td#middle").width(); 
		
		/* Images without caption */
		jQuery(".post img").each(function() { 
			var maxwidth = centerwidth - 10 + 'px';
			var imgwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var imgheight = jQuery(this).height(); 
			var newimgheight = (centerwidth / imgwidth * imgheight) + 'px';	
			if (imgwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxwidth}); 
				jQuery(this).css({height: newimgheight}); 
			}
		});
		
		/* Images with caption */
		jQuery("div.wp-caption").each(function() { 
			var captionwidth = jQuery(this).width(); 
			var maxcaptionwidth = centerwidth + 'px';
			var captionheight = jQuery(this).height();
			var captionimgwidth =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").width();
			var captionimgheight =  jQuery("div.wp-caption img").height();
			if (captionwidth > centerwidth) { 
				jQuery(this).css({width: maxcaptionwidth}); 
				var newcaptionheight = (centerwidth / captionwidth * captionheight) + 'px';
				var newcaptionimgheight = (centerwidth / captionimgwidth * captionimgheight) + 'px';
				jQuery(this).css({height: newcaptionheight}); 
				jQuery("div.wp-caption img").css({height: newcaptionimgheight}); 
				}
		});
		
		/* sfhover for LI:HOVER support in IE6: */
		jQuery("ul li").
			hover( function() {
					jQuery(this).addClass("sfhover")
				}, 
				function() {
					jQuery(this).removeClass("sfhover")
				} 
			); 

	/* End IE6 */
	}
	
	
	
	/* Since 3.7.8: Auto resize videos (embed and iframe elements) 
	TODO: Parse parent's dimensions only once per layout column, not per video
	*/
	function bfa_resize_video() {
		jQuery('embed, iframe').each( function() {
			var video = jQuery(this),
			videoWidth = video.attr('width'); // use the attr here, not width() or css()
			videoParent = video.parent(),
			videoParentWidth = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'width' ) ),
			videoParentBorder = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-left-width' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'border-right-width' ) ),
			videoParentPadding = parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-left' ) ) 
										+  parseFloat( videoParent.css( 'padding-right' ) ),
			maxWidth = videoParentWidth - videoParentBorder - videoParentPadding;

			if( videoWidth > maxWidth ) {
				var videoHeight = video.attr('height'),
				videoMaxHeight = ( maxWidth / videoWidth * videoHeight );
				video.attr({ width: maxWidth, height: videoMaxHeight });
			} 

		});	
	}
	bfa_resize_video();
	jQuery(window).resize( bfa_resize_video );

		
	jQuery(".post table tr").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("over");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("over");
		});

	
	jQuery(".post table tr:even").
		addClass("alt");

	
	jQuery("input.text, input.TextField, input.file, input.password, textarea").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("highlight"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("highlight"); 
		})
	
	jQuery("input.inputblur").
		focus(function () {  
			jQuery(this).addClass("inputfocus"); 
		}).
		blur(function () { 
			jQuery(this).removeClass("inputfocus"); 
		})

		

	
	jQuery("input.button, input.Button, input#submit").
		mouseover(function() {
			jQuery(this).addClass("buttonhover");
		}).
		mouseout(function() {
			jQuery(this).removeClass("buttonhover");
		});

	/* toggle "you can use these xhtml tags" */
	jQuery("a.xhtmltags").
		click(function(){ 
			jQuery("div.xhtml-tags").slideToggle(300); 
		});

	/* For the Tabbed Widgets plugin: */
	jQuery("ul.tw-nav-list").
		addClass("clearfix");

		
	
});

//]]>
</script>

		<!-- / Left Sidebar -->
		
				

		<!-- Main Column -->
		<td id="middle">

								<div class="post-183 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-cpp-tutorial odd" id="post-183">
						<div class="post-headline">		<h1>12.5 &#8212; The virtual table</h1>
		</div>		<div class="post-byline">By Alex, on February 8th, 2008</div>		<div class="post-bodycopy clearfix"><p>To implement virtual functions, C++ uses a special form of late binding known as the virtual table.  The <strong>virtual table</strong> is a lookup table of functions used to resolve function calls in a dynamic/late binding manner.  The virtual table sometimes goes by other names, such as &#8220;vtable&#8221;, &#8220;virtual function table&#8221;, &#8220;virtual method table&#8221;, or &#8220;dispatch table&#8221;.</p>
<p>Because knowing how the virtual table works is not necessary to use virtual functions, this section can be considered optional reading.</p>
<p>The virtual table is actually quite simple, though it&#8217;s a little complex to describe in words.  First, every class that uses virtual functions (or is derived from a class that uses virtual functions) is given it&#8217;s own virtual table.  This table is simply a static array that the compiler sets up at compile time.  A virtual table contains one entry for each virtual function that can be called by objects of the class.  Each entry in this table is simply a function pointer that points to the most-derived function accessible by that class.</p>
<p>Second, the compiler also adds a hidden pointer to the base class, which we will call *__vptr.  *__vptr is set (automatically) when a class instance is created so that it points to the virtual table for that class.  Unlike the *this pointer, which is actually a function parameter used by the compiler to resolve self-references, *__vptr is a real pointer.  Consequently, it makes each class object allocated bigger by the size of one pointer.  It also means that *__vptr is inherited by derived classes, which is important.</p>
<p>By now, you&#8217;re probably confused as to how these things all fit together, so let&#8217;s take a look at a simple example:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d7975b4adf845907554" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">

<p></p>
<p>Because there are 3 classes here, the compiler will set up 3 virtual tables: one for Base, one for D1, and one for D2.</p>
<p>The compiler also adds a hidden pointer to the most base class that uses virtual functions.  Although the compiler does this automatically, we&#8217;ll put it in the next example just to show where it&#8217;s added:</p>

				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-m">virtual</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">function2</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-7"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-8">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-9"><span class="crayon-t">class</span><span class="crayon-h"> class="crayon-e">Base</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-10"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-11"><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-12"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-m">virtual</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">function1</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-13"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-14">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-15"><span class="crayon-t">class</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">D2</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">Base</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-16"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-17"><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-18"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-m">virtual</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">function2</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4af0025989613-19"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0024 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>When a class object is created, *__vptr is set to point to the virtual table for that class.  For example, when a object of type Base is created, *__vptr is set to point to the virtual table for Base.  When objects of type D1 or D2 are constructed, *__vptr is set to point to the virtual table for D1 or D2 respectively.</p>
<p>Now, let&#8217;s talk about how these virtual tables are filled out.  Because there are only two virtual functions here, each virtual table will have two entries (one for function1(), and one for function2()).  Remember that when these virtual tables are filled out, each entry is filled out with the most-derived function an object of that class type can call.</p>
<p>Base&#8217;s virtual table is simple.  An object of type Base can only access the members of Base.  Base has no access to D1 or D2 functions.  Consequently, the entry for function1 points to Base::function1(), and the entry for function2 points to Base::function2().</p>
<p>D1&#8217;s virtual table is slightly more complex.  An object of type D1 can access members of both D1 and Base.  However, D1 has overridden function1(), making D1::function1() more derived than Base::function1().  Consequently, the entry for function1 points to D1::function1().  D1 hasn&#8217;t overridden function2(), so the entry for function2 will point to Base::function2().</p>
<p>D2&#8217;s virtual table is similar to D1, except the entry for function1 points to Base::function1(), and the entry for function2 points to D2::function2().</p>
<p>Here&#8217;s a picture of this graphically:</p>
<p><img src="http://www.learncpp.com/images/CppTutorial/Section12/VTable.gif"></p>
<p>Although this diagram is kind of crazy looking, it&#8217;s really quite simple: the *__vptr in each class points to the virtual table for that class.  The entries in the virtual table point to the most-derived version of the function objects of that class are allowed to call.</p>
<p>So consider what happens when we create an object of type D1:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-4">4</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">D1 </span><span class="crayon-v">cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4afa149012002-4"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0004 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Because cClass is a D1 object, cClass has it&#8217;s *__vptr set to the D1 virtual table.</p>
<p>Now, let&#8217;s set a base pointer to D1:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-5">5</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">D1 </span><span class="crayon-v">cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">Base</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pClass</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b00470944601-5"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0007 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>Note that because pClass is a base pointer, it only points to the Base portion of cClass.  However, also note that *__vptr is in the Base portion of the class, so pClass has access to this pointer.  Finally, note that pClass->__vptr points to the D1 virtual table!  Consequently, even though pClass is of type Base, it still has access to D1&#8217;s virtual table.</p>
<p>So what happens when we try to call pClass->function1()?</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-6">6</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">D1 </span><span class="crayon-v">cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">Base</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pClass</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">pClass</span><span class="crayon-o">-&gt;</span><span class="crayon-e">function1</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b07154762583-6"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>First, the program recognizes that function1() is a virtual function.  Second, uses pClass->__vptr to get to D1&#8217;s virtual table.  Third, it looks up which version of function1() to call in D1&#8217;s virtual table.  This has been set to D1::function1().  Therefore, pClass->function1() resolves to D1::function1()!</p>
<p>Now, you might be saying, &#8220;But what if Base really pointed to a Base object instead of a D1 object.  Would it still call D1::function1()?&#8221;.  The answer is no.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-5">5</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-6">6</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-2"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">Base </span><span class="crayon-v">cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">Base</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pClass</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">&amp;cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-5"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">pClass</span><span class="crayon-o">-&gt;</span><span class="crayon-e">function1</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b4b0e848409385-6"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>In this case, when cClass is created, __vptr points to Base&#8217;s virtual table, not D1&#8217;s virtual table.  Consequently, pClass->__vptr will also be pointing to Base&#8217;s virtual table.  Base&#8217;s virtual table entry for function1() points to Base::function1().  Thus, pClass->function1() resolves to Base::function1(), which is the most-derived version of function1() that a Base object should be able to call.</p>
<p>By using these tables, the compiler and program are able to ensure function calls resolve to the appropriate virtual function, even if you&#8217;re only using a pointer or reference to a base class!</p>
<p>Calling a virtual function is slower than calling a non-virtual function for a couple of reasons: First, we have to use the *__vptr to get to the appropriate virtual table.  Second, we have to index the virtual table to find the correct function to call.  Only then can we call the function.  As a result, we have to do 3 operations to find the function to call, as opposed to 2 operations for a normal indirect function call, or one operation for a direct function call.  However, with modern computers, this added time is usually fairly insignificant.</p>
<table border=0 cellpadding=3>
<tr>

		<div id="crayon-555d7975bbc64004339309" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">

					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975bbc64004339309-1">1</div><div <p></p>
<p>I thought this way: once D1::function2() isn&#8217;t at the VTable of D1, cause it&#8217;s not virtual, and it&#8217;s also not in the scope of Base class, the only function2() *pb can see is the Base::function2(), inherited from the own base.</p>
<p>But the result of this code is this:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>

				</td>

<p>How can this be possible?</p>

		<p>This brings up an interesting point.  Once a function is marked as virtual, it is considered virtual from that point on, regardless of whether the virtual keyword is used in derived classes or not.</p>
<p>Consider the following example:</p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

</span><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">Base</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-11"><span class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-13"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">go</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"D1"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-14"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-15">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-16"><span class="crayon-t">class</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">D2</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">D1</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-17"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-18"><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-19"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">go</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"D2"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-20"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-21">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-22"><span class="crayon-t">class</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">D3</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">D2</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-23"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-24"><span class="crayon-m">public</span><span class="crayon-o">:</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-25"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-t">void</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">go</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">cout</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-s">"D3"</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">&lt;&lt;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">endl</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-26"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-27">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-28">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-29"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-30"><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-31">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-32"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-v">Base</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">*</span><span class="crayon-v">pBase</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">D3</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-33"><span class="crayon-h">	</span><span class="crayon-v">pBase</span><span class="crayon-o">-&gt;</span><span class="crayon-e">go</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-c">// does this print base, D1, or D3?</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-34">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-35"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-st">return</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975bb811008457113-36"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0044 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>The answer is it prints D3.  Because go() was declared as virtual in Base, it&#8217;s considered virtual in Base, D1, D2, and D3.  Thus pBase->go() resolves all the way up to D3::go() in this case.</p>
		</div>

		<p>[code]<br />
//good example with out key word virtual */<br />
class Base<br />
{<br />
public :<br />
	  void go()<br />
	 {<br />
		 cout&lt;&lt;&quot;\n i am in base:&quot;;<br />
	 }<br />
};<br />
class D1 : public Base<br />
{<br />
public :<br />
	void go()<br />
	{<br />
		cout&lt;&lt;&quot;\n I am in d1:&quot;;<br />
	}<br />
};</p>
<p>class D2 : public Base<br />
{<br />
public :<br />
	        void go()<br />
			{<br />
				cout&lt;go();  // it will execute D2<br />
((D1*)ptr)-&gt;go();  // it will execute D1</p>
<p>return o;<br />
}</p>

class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-c">//It will call D1</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975ba296305332942-31">&nbsp;</div><div class="crayon-line </span><span class="crayon-cn">0</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975ba296305332942-35"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-42007">
		<div id="div-comment-42007" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/#comment-42007">
		February 6, 2009 at 12:17 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=42007#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-42007", "42007", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>You are incorrect.  The key is the following line: &#8220;When a class object is created, *__vptr is set to point to the virtual table for that class&#8221;</p>
<p>The virtual tables are constructed at compile time for each class, but the *__vptr pointer is set at run time based on what type of class is actually being instantiated.</p>
		</div>

		<li class="comment byuser comment-author-alex bypostauthor odd alt depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-59717">
		<div id="div-comment-59717" class="clearfix comment-container bypostauthor">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/a4e62d28c29f6c864923207d4c17993b?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://www.tarindel.com' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>Alex</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/#comment-59717">
		May 1, 2009 at 7:21 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=59717#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-59717", "59717", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to Alex'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>A derived class always has all the functionality of a base class, whereas the converse is not true.  So if you have a base pointer, whether you set it to a base class or a derived class, you&#8217;re guaranteed the functional in the base class is present and can be accessed through the base pointer.</p>
<p>However, if you have a derived pointer, what happens when you set it to point at a base class and then try and access something that only exists in the derived class?  It wouldn&#8217;t know what to do.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		</div>
		<p>Thanks Alex for nice explanation.</p>
<p>I have one doubt.<br />
As per your explanation &#8220;when a object of type Base<br />
is created, *__vptr is set to point to the virtual<br />
table for Base.&#8221;.</p>
<p>But if I create 3 objects of type Base, as per your<br />
statement *__vptr is set to point to the virtual<br />
table for Base 3 times. But what is the need of<br />
setting __*vptr 3 times? Virtual table address<br />
should be same for all the 3 times.</p>
		</div>
<ul class="children">
		<li class="comment even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-62259">
		<div id="div-comment-62259" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/ba811e3f04f88aaa2c6a987ffa3b3dc7?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/ba811e3f04f88aaa2c6a987ffa3b3dc7?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Sumit</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/#comment-62259">
		June 11, 2009 at 1:31 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=62259#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-62259", "62259", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to Sumit'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>&#8220;vptr&#8221; cannot be static because if it were, it would be shared by all( as you said)<br />
but when a base class object is made to instantiate a derived class object, the &#8220;vptr&#8221; then points to the v-table of the derived.therefore we need the vptr to point to different v-tables as per the context.</p>
<p>therefore vptr is not shared by objects(static), else they would had already done that <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /><br />
PS: v-tables are static for a class</p>
		</div>

		<p>Reply for &#8220;Comment by Siva Prasad. S &#8221;<br />
Abstract class cannot create object. Creating a pointer of abstract base class can only point to derived classes. So, the _vptr can in any case will point to only derived class vtable.</p>

		<li class="comment odd alt thread-even depth-1 clearfix" id="comment-73193">
		<div id="div-comment-73193" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/1de11b7184bc04ae1b3516d49ec118c6?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://1.gravatar.com/avatar/1de11b7184bc04ae1b3516d49ec118c6?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Calista</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/#comment-73193">
		November 27, 2009 at 4:45 pm</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=73193#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-73193", "73193", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to Calista'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Yes, the vtable entry will be NULL. If you think about it, a pure virtual function in a class makes it abstract which means we can never instantiate the class - which means we can&#8217;t call that function directly or indirectly from any base\derived class objects (we can&#8217;t create base class objects anyway and in case of derived class, if you define the &#8220;pure virtual function&#8221; of base class then you have provided the implementation. And if you don&#8217;t - then the derived class in turn becomes an abstract class. And so it goes on and on.</p>
<p>To cut it short - yes, it will have NULL. Then you might ask who is going to invoke the NULL function? Not me. No one can call it and it also wastes memory. So Microsoft came with its own invention for that, when you declare a class with __declspec(novtable) for abstract base classes - you are effectively saying - &#8220;I know what I am doing. I don&#8217;t want to declare the vtable for this abstract base class, since no one can instantiate an object of this class anyway. So please save some memory and donot construct the vtable. Thank you&#8221;.</p>
<p>Also consider C# - to declare a class as abstract all you have to do is:<br />
&#8220;abstact class IAmIntuitiveAbstractClassDeclaration&#8221;</p>
<p>Isn&#8217;t that intuitive instead of define virtual function, and then make that virtual function &#8220;pure&#8221; - = 0? I might have as well said &#8220;you can declare an abstract base class by making one of the virutal functions a zombie and declare it like this </p>
<p>&#8220;virtual void laspseInDesign const = Zombie&#8221; Seems ad hoc to me.</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		<li class="comment even depth-2 clearfix" id="comment-74907">
		<div id="div-comment-74907" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c8c15c9688fdacb56c7e5100bfec52f0?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/c8c15c9688fdacb56c7e5100bfec52f0?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname"><a href='http://no' rel='external nofollow' class='url'>color</a></span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/#comment-74907">
		December 26, 2009 at 4:44 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=74907#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-74907", "74907", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to color'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Please careful experience the following words.</p>
<p>Because cClass is a D1 object, cClass has its *__vptr set to the D1 virtual table.<br />
And then you set a base pointer to D1.<br />
Because pClass is a base pointer, <strong>it only points to the Base portion of cClass</strong>. However, also note that <strong>*__vptr is in the Base portion of the class</strong>.  so pClass has access to this pointer. Finally, note that pClass-&gt;__vptr points to the D1 virtual table!</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

		<div id="div-comment-76705" class="clearfix comment-container">

		<img alt='' src='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/81a66efef6eb7898a9cee3ca13d7ee5a?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://2.gravatar.com/avatar/81a66efef6eb7898a9cee3ca13d7ee5a?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Paras Jatkar</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/#comment-76705">
		January 18, 2010 at 1:38 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=76705#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-76705", "76705", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to Paras Jatkar'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>Object allocation in the memory will be done at run time and assignment of that allocated memory address can be assigned only at Run time.<br />
This will happen at the Run time and hence called &#8216;Late binding&#8217;.</p>
<p>Its a nice Explanation from the original author..<br />
Good Job! <img src="http://www.learncpp.com/blog/wp-includes/images/smilies/simple-smile.png" alt=":-)" class="wp-smiley" style="height: 1em; max-height: 1em;" /></p>
		</div>

		<p>ALEX, Thanks a lot&#8230;for helping many of us to understand &#8216;vtables&#8217;.</p>
<p>Q: can any one let me know if we can display the &#8216;vtable&#8217; for a class? If yes, HOW?</p>
<p> ref : &#8216;http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Virtual_method_table&#8217;. Here they are displaying the vtable for a class as below : </p>
<p>&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;&gt;<br />
G++ 3.4.6 from GCC produces the following 32 bit memory layout for the object b2:[nb 1]</p>
<p>b2:<br />
  +0: pointer to virtual method table of B2<br />
  +4: value of int_in_b2</p>
<p>virtual method table of B2:<br />
  +0: B2::f2()<br />
&lt;&lt;&lt;&lt;&lt;&lt;&lt;&lt;&lt;&lt;<br />
-thnx,<br />
Vijay Chulaki</p>

</span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-r">new</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">D2</span><span <p></p>
<p>most compilers will do somewhat like this: The vtable is placed in the object file with the definition of the first non-pure, non-inline, virtual function of the class (classAf.o in this example) with external linkage.</p>
<p>But what if we have:</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<p>useA1() and useA2() must have access to the vtable of class A, but where is it defined, since the compiler rule from previous example does not match here?</p>
<p>In can be defined in both useA1.cpp and useA2.cpp, but than it must have static linkage.</p>
<p>Right or do I miss something?</p>

		</div>
		<p>Hi</p>
<p>it can&#8217;t be static because it will change the address according to the allocation.</p>
<p>C1 *cClass= new C1();<br />
D1 *dClass= new D1();<br />
Base *pClass = &dClass;<br />
Base *p1Class= &cClass;</p>
<p>vptr of pClass instance is pointing D1 vtable<br />
vptr of p1Class instance is pointing C1 vtable</p>
		</div>

		<p>Heading : Non virtual function of base class is getting executed though it is overridden<br />
          in the derived class.</p>
<p>Please find the code sample below.</p>
<p>class vehicle<br />
{<br />
	public:<br />
	    virtual void speed()<br />
		{<br />
			cout &lt;&lt; &quot;In base speed&quot; &lt;&lt; &quot;\n&quot;;<br />
		}</p>
<p>		virtual void maintain()<br />
		{<br />
			cout &lt;&lt; &quot;In base maintain&quot; &lt;&lt; &quot;\n&quot;;<br />
		}</p>
<p>		void value()<br />
		{<br />
			cout &lt;&lt; &quot;In base value&quot; &lt;&lt; &quot;\n&quot;;<br />
		}</p>
<p>};</p>
<p>class wheel4 : public vehicle<br />
{<br />
public:<br />
		virtual void speed()<br />
		{<br />
			cout &lt;&lt; &quot;In 4wheel speed&quot; &lt;&lt; &quot;\n&quot;;<br />
		}</p>
<p>		virtual void maintain()<br />
		{<br />
			cout &lt;&lt; &quot;In 4wheel maintain&quot; &lt;&lt; &quot;\n&quot;;<br />
		}</p>
<p>		void value()<br />
		{<br />
			cout &lt;&lt; &quot;In wheel4 value&quot; &lt;value();<br />
}<br />
After the execution of ptr-&gt;value(), the function present in the class &#8220;vehicle&#8221; is<br />
getting executed.  As per my understanding the &#8220;value&#8221; present in wheel4 should<br />
be executed.</p>
<p>What is the reason for this?</p>

		<div id="div-comment-88894" class="clearfix comment-container">
		<div class="comment-author vcard">
		<img alt='' src='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f95f4dcdf315e3a90663e8ad6395fa1e?s=65&#038;d=mm&#038;r=g' srcset='http://0.gravatar.com/avatar/f95f4dcdf315e3a90663e8ad6395fa1e?s=130&amp;d=mm&amp;r=g 2x' class='avatar avatar-65 photo' height='65' width='65' />		<span class="authorname">Deepu Abraham K</span>
		</div>
				<div class="comment-meta commentmetadata">
		<a href="http://www.learncpp.com/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/#comment-88894">
		July 22, 2010 at 1:53 am</a>
        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=88894#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-88894", "88894", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to Deepu Abraham K'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>As Alex had stated in the above diagram,</p>
<p>When you do<br />
vehicle* vobj = new wheel4;<br />
here what happens is *ONLY* the *__vptr of vehicle class will get updated with the vtable of wheel4.</p>
<p>remember that you have only one function in the virtual table i.e, void speed()</p>
<p>if you want to print &#8220;In wheel4 value&#8221; make the void value() function in the vehicle class as  virtual void value() by doing this you are adding this function into the virtual table..</p>
<p>the crux of this revolves around the *__vptr getting filled by the vtable pointer.This is how c++ obtains the dynamism which it claims. </p>
<p>Hope this clear the air !</p>
		</div>
</li><!-- #comment-## -->

<p></p>
<p>when doing a copy by value :</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

		<div id="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591" class="crayon-syntax crayon-theme-familiar-learncppcom crayon-font-monaco crayon-os-pc print-yes notranslate" data-settings=" no-popup minimize scroll-mouseover wrap" style=" margin-top: 12px; margin-bottom: 12px; font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;">
		
			<div class="crayon-plain-wrap"></div>
			<div class="crayon-main" style="">
				<table class="crayon-table">
					<tr class="crayon-row">
				<td class="crayon-nums " data-settings="show">
					<div class="crayon-nums-content" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important;"><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-1">1</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-2">2</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-3">3</div><div class="crayon-num crayon-striped-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-4">4</div><div class="crayon-num" data-line="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-5">5</div></div>
				</td>
						<td class="crayon-code"><div class="crayon-pre" style="font-size: 12px !important; line-height: 15px !important; -moz-tab-size:4; -o-tab-size:4; -webkit-tab-size:4; tab-size:4;"><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-1"><span class="crayon-t">int</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-e">main</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-sy">{</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-2"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">D1 </span><span class="crayon-v">cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-3"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-e">Base </span><span class="crayon-v">pClass</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-o">=</span><span class="crayon-h"> </span><span class="crayon-v">cClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line crayon-striped-line" id="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-4"><span class="crayon-h">&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;&nbsp;</span><span class="crayon-v">pClass</span><span class="crayon-sy">.</span><span class="crayon-e">function1</span><span class="crayon-sy">(</span><span class="crayon-sy">)</span><span class="crayon-sy">;</span></div><div class="crayon-line" id="crayon-555d7975b94e2094248591-5"><span class="crayon-sy">}</span></div></div></td>
					</tr>
				</table>
			</div>
		</div>
<!-- [Format Time: 0.0009 seconds] -->
<p></p>
<p>the displayed result is &#8220;Base::function1&#8243; .<br />
I thought it should be &#8220;D1::function1&#8243; as *__vptr points to D1 virtual table.</p>
<p>So why it calls Base::function1 ?</p>

		<p>@toto</p>
<p>pClass is initialized with Base&#8217;s vtable.<br />
Virtual Table&#8217;s are not copied.</p>
<p></p><!-- Crayon Syntax Highlighter v2.7.1 -->

<p></p>
<p>would however invoke D1:function1 as pClass refers/points to cClass which had its *__vptr to be initialized to D1&#8217;s vtable.</p>

		<p>Hi,<br />
i wanted to know the order of functions how it is stored in the vtable.<br />
ex:<br />
class Base<br />
{<br />
 public:<br />
 virtual void function1() {};<br />
 virtual void function2() {};<br />
};  </p>
<p>class D1: public Base<br />
{<br />
public:<br />
  virtual void function3() {};<br />
  virtual void function4() {};<br />
};  </p>
<p>how will the vtable for D1 look like?<br />
is it - function1()<br />
        function2()<br />
        function3()<br />
        function4()</p>
<p>         or<br />
        function3()<br />
        function4()<br />
        function1()<br />
        function2()</p>
<p>Thanks in advance</p>

        <span class="comment-reply-link"><a class='comment-reply-link' href='/cpp-tutorial/125-the-virtual-table/?replytocom=95580#respond' onclick='return addComment.moveForm( "comment-95580", "95580", "respond", "183" )' aria-label='Reply to ajloeffl'> &middot; Reply</a></span>		 
		</div>
		<p>sapnads,</p>
<p>All you are doing is making a base pointer (pClass) that points to an already created derived class (D1).  This is standard practice and the *__vpr points to the virtual function table for a D1 object type.</p>
